# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

62-assistanttext-
I've successfully completed the analysis and created the `/workspace/answer.json` file with comprehensive findings about OpenTelemetry span creation patterns.

## Summary of Findings:

### **Prometheus/Prometheus** uses:
- **Global tracer access**: `otel.Tracer("")` directly from the OpenTelemetry package
- **Span patterns**: `ctx, span := otel.Tracer("").Start(ctx, "operation_name")`
- **Attributes**: `span.SetAttributes(attribute.Int(...), attribute.String(...))`
- **Span kind**: `trace.WithSpanKind(trace.SpanKindClient)` for network operations
- **Context access**: `trace.SpanFromContext(ctx)` to get existing spans
- **Files with examples**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, `storage/remote/client.go`, `scrape/scrape.go`, `rules/group.go`

### **Grafana/Grafana** uses:
- **Service-based initialization**: `TracingService` with Jaeger exporter configuration
- **Dependency injection**: Tracer obtained via `otel.GetTracerProvider().Tracer("service-name")`
- **Rich error handling**: Consistent use of both `span.RecordError(err)` AND `span.SetStatus(codes.Error, msg)`
- **Attribute patterns**: Uses both `trace.WithAttributes()` at creation and `span.SetAttributes()` post-creation
- **Semantic conventions**: Extensively uses `semconv` for HTTP and standard attributes
- **Files with examples**: `pkg/infra/tracing/tracing.go`, `pkg/tsdb/tempo/metrics_stream.go`, `pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/tracing_middleware.go`

The answer document includes **39 relevant files**, **9 key symbols**, and **8 call chain entries** with a detailed narrative explaining all patterns and differences.

`semconv \\\"go.opentelemetry.io/otel/semconv/v1.17.0\\\"`\\n- HTTP attributes: `semconv.HTTPURL()`, `semconv.HTTPMethod()`, `semconv.HTTPStatusCode()`, `semconv.HTTPResendCount()`\\n- `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:611` - Outer span contains inner loop with pattern-specific spans\\n- `pkg/registry/apis/dashboard/datasources.go` - Spans created from context passed through function calls\\n- Prometheus uses span context for logging: `rules/group.go:527-528` - Extract and log trace ID\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Tracer Initialization:** Prometheus uses global `otel.Tracer(\\\"\\\")` directly, while Grafana initializes through `TracingService` with dependency injection via Wire\\n2. **Error Handling:** Grafana consistently pairs `RecordError()` with `SetStatus()`, while Prometheus mostly omits error handling in traced operations\\n3. **Semantic Conventions:** Grafana uses more structured semantic conventions for HTTP (v1.17.0), while Prometheus uses them selectively\\n4. **Span Kind:** Both use `trace.WithSpanKind()`, particularly for client operations\\n5. **Attribute Timing:** Grafana uses both `trace.WithAttributes()` at creation and `SetAttributes()` post-creation, while Prometheus primarily uses post-creation `SetAttributes()`\"\n}\n",
